<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_12181509">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/12181509" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/763116-selena" class="left imgcol" title="Selena"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1399263258p2/763116.jpg" alt="Selena" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/12181509?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 10, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/763116-selena" class="user" title="Selena">Selena</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/568628.The_Cat_Who_Wasn_t_There" title="Paperback 9780515111279" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who needs a mental break</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/763116-selena?shelf=just-plain-fun" class="actionLinkLite">just-plain-fun</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer12181509">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5047890267352083351">I'm only going to bother reviewing one of the "Cat Who..." books, so just consider this a general review of the whole series, I'm just using The Cat Who Wasn't There to do it because it was the first one I read. Since high school, these books have been my cheesy, fun, light-reading (yet with enough classical references to actually keep me occupied), something to do when I felt like reading, needed my mind occupied, but just didn't feel the energy needed to foucus on the new translation of Dante</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5047890267352083351">I'm only going to bother reviewing one of the "Cat Who..." books, so just consider this a general review of the whole series, I'm just using The Cat Who Wasn't There to do it because it was the first one I read. Since high school, these books have been my cheesy, fun, light-reading (yet with enough classical references to actually keep me occupied), something to do when I felt like reading, needed my mind occupied, but just didn't feel the energy needed to foucus on the new translation of Dante (or whatever). They're great, they're fun, witty enough to keep me occupied and I'm willing to admit that I still pick one up from time to time, especially during the summer. ;o)<br /><br />The series centers on a tiny town ("400 miles north of everywhere," as every book begins) and a retired big-city reporter who moved up there after inheriting an unexpected fortune from a distant relative. He and his cats solve mysteries while being surrounded by a quirky town with lots of quirky people...and yep, thats pretty much the whole thing. Go ahead, make fun of me if you must. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5047890267352083351">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/255997656?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 07, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5581493-kirsti" class="user" title="Kirsti">Kirsti</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/568628.The_Cat_Who_Wasn_t_There" title="Paperback 9780515111279" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Cat lovers, Mystery lovers, Animal detective fans</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5581493-kirsti?shelf=cozy-cat-murder-mysteries" class="actionLinkLite">cozy-cat-murder-mysteries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer255997656">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer505718632212178982">I have to say, I miss the part of the book where Koko wasn't there, although he was making his presence felt. You come to depend on his Yows and Yargles signalling clues, and he is giving them, you just don't realize it.<br /><br />Qwill has been persuaded to look into his Scottish heritage by joining a Pickaxe tour group. While there, Irma Hasselreich dies mysteriously. The truth comes out after Koko's obsession with Melinda Goodwinter and pink pills. It was odd seeing Melinda portrayed as she was, so mone</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText505718632212178982">I have to say, I miss the part of the book where Koko wasn't there, although he was making his presence felt. You come to depend on his Yows and Yargles signalling clues, and he is giving them, you just don't realize it.<br /><br />Qwill has been persuaded to look into his Scottish heritage by joining a Pickaxe tour group. While there, Irma Hasselreich dies mysteriously. The truth comes out after Koko's obsession with Melinda Goodwinter and pink pills. It was odd seeing Melinda portrayed as she was, so money hungry. She was slightly annoying in previous books, but just more so in this one.<br /><br />Another Cat Who read in one sitting, this time before bed. I had to keep reading until the end, even though I've read this series before. They are just addictive, and you find yourself drawn in and caring for or hating the characters accordingly. They really are just that good!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="505718632212178982">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1018205610">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1018205610" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8391431-m-j" class="left imgcol" title="M. J."><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1332730259p2/8391431.jpg" alt="M. J." /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1018205610?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 14, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8391431-m-j" class="user" title="M. J.">M. J.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/568628.The_Cat_Who_Wasn_t_There" title="Paperback 9780515111279" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8391431-m-j?shelf=read-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">read-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1018205610">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10216526994581186749">I described the circumstances of my reading this book in my review of The Cat Who Could Read Backwards <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1019782954?book_show_action=false" target="_blank">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> so I'll keep it brief here. My reading was interrupted by my wife grabbing the book, and when I attempted to recover it I instead found the first in the series, which I read and reviewed. For a while I was reading whichever I could find, but I managed to focus on finishing that one, and then turned to this one.<br /><br />It occurred to me at some point that the tit</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10216526994581186749">I described the circumstances of my reading this book in my review of The Cat Who Could Read Backwards <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1019782954?book_show_action=false" target="_blank">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> so I'll keep it brief here. My reading was interrupted by my wife grabbing the book, and when I attempted to recover it I instead found the first in the series, which I read and reviewed. For a while I was reading whichever I could find, but I managed to focus on finishing that one, and then turned to this one.<br /><br />It occurred to me at some point that the titular cat, Koko, somehow had gotten very old. I've had many cats, none of which have lived two decades, and Koko was by this point well beyond that age. Yet he is a very active cat who still dashes about the house when excited and leaps tall furniture in a single bound. Given that the first book was published in the mid to late sixties and this in the early mid nineties, and Koko was not a kitten in the first book, that's an extraordinary age for a cat. But then, it's a fictional cat in a fictional story.<br /><br />In the series between these two points, news reporter Qwilleran somehow became the sole heir of a fortune. He did not really want to be ridiculously wealthy, so he put most of it in a foundation, although he lives well with his now two cats (Yum-Yum is not nearly so remarkable as Koko, but she is an affectionate animal) in a converted apple barn furnished by an interior decorator. He is still the wealthiest person in this small community, despite the fact that there are still remnants of founding families who made millions in nineteenth century lumbering and mining in the cold northern Midwest. He is seeing the local librarian Polly, but is considered something of the region's most eligible bachelor.<br /><br />A young doctor, daughter of the doctor who had been town physician for decades, comes back to town after his death, apparently to take over his practice. She apparently also had been an old flame of Qwilleran; I'm not certain whether this is in a previous book or backstory created for this one. She seems fairly focused on restoring that relationship, which Qwill wants to avoid, making for some awkward interactions. Meanwhile, the local theatre company (funded by Qwill's foundation) is preparing to perform Macbeth, and one of Polly's friends suggests that key members of the cast and others ought to take a brief tour of Scotland.<br /><br />Polly has been bothered by a stalker, and Qwill is concerned that the stalker is intending to kidnap her and hold her for ransom; thus he encourages the trip and travels with them. Then on one eventful morning the friend who planned and was leading the tour died overnight of what the doctor claimed was a heart attack, the bus driver vanished, and the luggage of one of the travelers, containing several hundred thousand dollars in jewelry, was stolen. Qwill can't help thinking that the woman was murdered and that the theft was somehow connected, particularly since his cat sitter reports that Koko let out a terrible wail in the middle of the night, at just about the time the woman must have died on the other side of the ocean.<br /><br />Things continue to be strange upon their return home. Koko defaces pictures of the doctor's daughter and complains at her voice on the reporter's recordings, but he has always disliked her. The stalker is seen again, and seen stealing small valuables. The entire contents of the doctor's home are sold by a local auctioneer in a tag sale on the premises. The woman who was robbed of the jewelry was robbed again of a very valuable collection. Macbeth goes off fairly well. Ultimately the mystery is solved, and Qwill is the one who works out the details thanks in part to Koko's antics. There is some exciting action along the way.<br /><br />I was uncomfortable about one point, what I consider a breach of the rules of mysteries. I felt as if once or twice the author indicated that the detective knew something, saw something, heard something that brought him closer to the answer--but we were not told what it was. A mystery is something of a puzzle, and keeping pieces from the reader is wrong. On the other hand, I would have to admit that at least one of the clues might have been mentioned in passing and overlooked by me. It is of course genuine mystery writing skill to be able to place important clues in places where they would be overlooked. This was probably a better mystery than I credit, and although I suspected all the right people I never managed to put together the right motives.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10216526994581186749">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Qwilleran returns to Pickaxe when he hears about a mysterious man who was hiding around his romantic interest Polly when she came home one night. Qwill senses something is wrong and suspects that someone intends to kidnap his friend to then extort money from him.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText15218579907580403807">This book starts exactly after the storyline in: The Cat Who Moved A Mountain. Qwilleran returns to Pickaxe when he hears about a mysterious man who was hiding around his romantic interest Polly when she came home one night. Qwill senses something is wrong and suspects that someone intends to kidnap his friend to then extort money from him. Sounds crazy, but the 'stache knows!<br /><br />Upon returning to Pickax ahead of schedule he meets up with friends and finds the town the same and yet changed a bit. The local Doctor has committed suicide and his daughter (also a Dr.) returns to take over his practice. She and Qwill have a "past." And she comes on strong to try and re-ignite their relationship. At the same time, a trip to Scotland is put together and Qwill decides to join in... then finds out both Polly and this new Doc are going. sigh.<br /><br />This mystery is an assemblage of events that don't add up right to Qwill and little by little he finds the truth beneath the surface, and it's not a pretty picture.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1141565593">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17547192649129940501">I think this is right in the era when the author starts to realize her particular brand of cheese and starts to play into it. The Cat Who Moved a Mountain was kind of testing the waters (could there be more potato puns?), but this one evens out the cheese factor with a *slightly* more complex plot than the other novels. It pulls in old plots and characters that keeps that great tight knit community feel in her world building, and adds new characters which allow for the plot to take place in mult</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17547192649129940501">I think this is right in the era when the author starts to realize her particular brand of cheese and starts to play into it. The Cat Who Moved a Mountain was kind of testing the waters (could there be more potato puns?), but this one evens out the cheese factor with a *slightly* more complex plot than the other novels. It pulls in old plots and characters that keeps that great tight knit community feel in her world building, and adds new characters which allow for the plot to take place in multiple locations (Moose County AND Scotland!) and even gives a faint wisp of a B-plot (a kidnapper! two women fighting for Qwill!) But for all the cheese and the technical weakness, this one is one of the more fun novels in the series. Recommended to anyone who's read the first 13 books in the series. :)</span>

      <a href="/user/show/3830946-sue" class="user" title="Sue">Sue</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3830946-sue?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer442477467">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3625941484290482359"> Qwill's lady-friend Polly lets him know about about a group trip planned to Scotland and invites him to go along. Polly's friend Irma, who reportedly has connections in Scotland, is organizing the trip and will serve as tour guide. The first few days of the tour are a blur of riding through the countryside listening to Irma tell stories about the area. Tragedy strikes Day Six of the trip when Irma dies in the night from an apparent heart attack. Several people abandon the trip at that point, wi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3625941484290482359"> Qwill's lady-friend Polly lets him know about about a group trip planned to Scotland and invites him to go along. Polly's friend Irma, who reportedly has connections in Scotland, is organizing the trip and will serve as tour guide. The first few days of the tour are a blur of riding through the countryside listening to Irma tell stories about the area. Tragedy strikes Day Six of the trip when Irma dies in the night from an apparent heart attack. Several people abandon the trip at that point, with more a few days later - Polly and Qwill among them. Back in Pickax, Koko starts acting strange as soon as Qwill returns. But Qwill is also concerned about what appears to be someone stalking Polly. Of course it takes a bit for Qwill to pick up on all the signals that Koko is sending him for him to get to the truth of Irma's cause of death.<br /> Started this as Hurricane Sandy raged outside - a good diversion to the storm - and finished the next day in the storm's aftermath. Light read, as always, with a good mix of the regular characters and small town happenings.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_230447302">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230447302" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6762578-cherry" class="left imgcol" title="Cherry"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1319425767p2/6762578.jpg" alt="Cherry" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/230447302?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 02, 2011</a>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer4687918314504885596">Like all the other books in the series, this book held me in suspense. It is about yet another of Jim Qwilleran's mysteries, in which this one was how the leader of the Bonnie Scotts Tour was murdered by one of the tourists. In the end, the answer was very surprising.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText4687918314504885596">Like all the other books in the series, this book held me in suspense. It is about yet another of Jim Qwilleran's mysteries, in which this one was how the leader of the Bonnie Scotts Tour was murdered by one of the tourists. In the end, the answer was very surprising. Melinda Goodwinter really likes Qwilleran, but he doesn't really like her that much. But the reason she likes him is because she hopes to marry him into the Klingshoen fortune. She notices that he doesn't like her that much, and does some snooping around. She finds out that he really really likes Polly Duncan, so she sets out to get rid of her. At the time, Polly was also on the Bonnie Scotts Tour with the leader, Irma Hasselrich. Polly was taking pills for her cardiovascular problems, but then the doctor prescribed her to a different pill. She gave the original pills to Irma. But Melinda didn't know that, and then she exchanged the original pills with a drugged type of pill, meaning to drug Polly. But then Irma took those drugged pills, and died in her sleep that night, while Polly wasn't harmed at all. Then, because Melinda felt so, so guilty about killing Irma, that she wrote a sorry note to Qwilleran, and 2 nights later, drove her car intentionally into one of the statues in Goodwinter Boulevard. She died.</span>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4437424-abbey?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer14936295541776950547">BOTTOM LINE: Qwill visits Scotland and, of course, bad things happen. This 14th in the long series has a comfortable, and rather satisfying plot (if a wee bit too coincidental), but while the latest stories were unbearably "cute!!", at this point they're still well-plotted, and worthwhile. <br /><br />Polly’s got a stalker, the lovely Melinda is back in town (and pushing for marriage), and somebody steals YumYum - seems Qwill just doesn’t have any luck with the females in his life, unless it’s bad. And on a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14936295541776950547">BOTTOM LINE: Qwill visits Scotland and, of course, bad things happen. This 14th in the long series has a comfortable, and rather satisfying plot (if a wee bit too coincidental), but while the latest stories were unbearably "cute!!", at this point they're still well-plotted, and worthwhile. <br /><br />Polly’s got a stalker, the lovely Melinda is back in town (and pushing for marriage), and somebody steals YumYum - seems Qwill just doesn’t have any luck with the females in his life, unless it’s bad. And on a vacation trip to Scotland one of the tour participants dies en.route, expensive jewelry is stolen, and his friends are acting oddly. <br /><br />While the characters are still interesting the tone of the series is getting sweeter, almost (but not quite) overwhelmingly so here - all Qwill’s friends are wonderful, nice, kindly and all the bad guys have few redeeming qualities. The sketchiness in character delineation is a weakness that is, I suspect, only going to worsen in the following novels. Too bad - this was a very well-written series earlier on. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_122412872">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122412872" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas" class="left imgcol" title="Benjamin Thomas"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451660582p2/4209082.jpg" alt="Benjamin Thomas" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/122412872?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 19, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas" class="user" title="Benjamin Thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/568628.The_Cat_Who_Wasn_t_There" title="Paperback 9780515111279" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=mystery-ameteur-sleuth" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-ameteur-sleuth</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer122412872">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4576377652873504868">I was due for a straight who-dunnit mystery and I also needed to read a shorter novel after just completing the lengthy "The Seventh Scroll". This book is the 15th in the "Cat Who..." series and although I haven't read all of them up to this point I would guess I have completed about 10-11 of them. I confess to not having read them in order, something I normally never do, but that is due to the nature of how I acquire them. You see I received several as gifts, years ago and I knew my mother had</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4576377652873504868">I was due for a straight who-dunnit mystery and I also needed to read a shorter novel after just completing the lengthy "The Seventh Scroll". This book is the 15th in the "Cat Who..." series and although I haven't read all of them up to this point I would guess I have completed about 10-11 of them. I confess to not having read them in order, something I normally never do, but that is due to the nature of how I acquire them. You see I received several as gifts, years ago and I knew my mother had read them and liked them so I gave them a try. Since then I occasionally pick one up at a used book store but by no means own all of them nor read them in the correct order. That really doesn't matter though as each is a stand alone story and the parts of the bigger story arc that stretch across books are slow moving and easily picked up by the context of each book.<br /><br />I do enjoy these novels...the more of them I read the more I enjoy them. They are safe mysteries, meaning I know what I'm getting each time I read one. I envy the main character's position in life: wealthy due to unexpected inheritance, yet living somewhat frugally in a small town filled with quirky characters. He writes a column in the local newspaper on topics he thinks are interesting. Really, it's a stress free life...or should be. The problem is, just like other who- dunnit protagonists, there are a lot of murders that seem to take place in his small town, and with the assistance of his two siamese cats, he usually gets into the middle of it.<br /><br />This particular entry in the series is among the favorites of the fans. It's easy to see why. Quill (Jim Quilleran, the protagonist), agrees to travel to Scotland with several of the townspeople and see the sites. This gets him out of the normal town routines and gives readers a change of scenery. The actual murder and subsequent mystery and the solving thereof takes many twists and turns as we travel with Quill to Scotland and back home again. His girlfriend is being stalked by an unknown person(s) and Quill himself is being stalked by an old flame intent upon marriage. Could she have her eye on that vast fortune of his? The town's character and it's quirky residents are on full display. All in all a witty story well told. I will keep on reading these books at a rate of 1-2 per year because its always nice to come home to a friendly place.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4576377652873504868">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Melinda Goodwinter was an old girlfriend of Qwill's, and she has just come back due to her father's death. She begins pestering him, making suggestive invitations, and finally tells him she wants to marry him. Qwill politely refuses.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/21625.Lilian_Jackson_Braun">About Lilian Jackson Braun</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/21625.Lilian_Jackson_Braun"><img alt="21625" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1206733773p2/21625.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer8661637090024756892">Lilian Jackson Braun was an American writer. She is well-known for her light-hearted series of <em>The Cat Who...</em> mystery novels. The <em>Cat Who</em> books center around the life of former newspaper reporter James Qwilleran, and his two Siamese cats, KoKo and Yum Yum in the fictitious small town of Pickax located in Moose County, "400 miles north of everywhere." Although never formally stated in the books, th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8661637090024756892">Lilian Jackson Braun was an American writer. She is well-known for her light-hearted series of <em>The Cat Who...</em> mystery novels. The <em>Cat Who</em> books center around the life of former newspaper reporter James Qwilleran, and his two Siamese cats, KoKo and Yum Yum in the fictitious small town of Pickax located in Moose County, "400 miles north of everywhere." Although never formally stated in the books, the towns, counties and lifestyles described in the series are generally accepted to be a modeled after Bad Axe, Michigan (located in the "Michigan Thumb") where she resided with her husband for many years until the mid 1980's. Many also believe that the culture and history of the Upper peninsula of Michigan are represented in the series as well, which is quite possible as it is indeed a fictitious location.<br /><br />Lilian Jackson Braun began her writing career as a teenager, contributing sports poetry for the <em>Detroit News</em>. She later began working as an advertising copywriter for many of Detroit's department stores. After that stint, she worked at the Detroit Free Press as the "Good Living" editor for 30 years. She retired from the Free Press in 1978.<br /><br />Between 1966 and 1968, she published three novels to critical acclaim: <em>The Cat Who Could Read Backwards, The Cat Who Ate Danish Modern</em> and <em>The Cat Who Turned On and Off</em>. In 1966, <em>The New York Times</em> labeled Braun, "the new detective of the year." The rising mystery author disappeared from the publishing scene for 18 years. The blame came from the fact that mystery novels were starting to focus on sex, violence, and foul language, and Braun's light-hearted books were not welcome in this new territory. It wasn't until 1986 that the Berkley Publishing Group reintroduced Braun to the public with the publication of an original paperback, <em>The Cat Who Saw Red</em>. Within two years, Berkeley released four new novels in paperback and reprinted the three mysteries from the sixties. Braun's series became an instant best seller once again. In January 2007 the twenty-ninth novel in the series, <em>The Cat Who Had 60 Whiskers</em>, was released in hardcover by the Penguin Group.<br /><br />Not much was really known about Braun, as she prefered to keep her private life that way. For years, publishers have given inaccurate accounts of her year of birth, which has remained unknown until she openly acknowledged her age in an interview for the Detroit News in January 2005.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8661637090024756892">...more</a>

    </div>
